Abu Hashim's Balance View
Abu Hashim introduces the balance method for nullification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Abu Hashim's proposal for balancing acts of obedience and sins to determine nullification, and how it avoids the problem of arbitrarily preferring one equal over another.

Core Idea
Balance avoids contradiction by nullifying an equal amount from the preponderant side.

Abu Hashim (founder of the Bahshamiyya school of Mu'tazila) offered a nuanced solution to the problem of how competing deserts for reward and punishment can cancel each other. He proposes weighing acts, where the preponderant side nullifies an equal amount from the other, leaving a surplus. This cleverly avoids having to choose between two equal claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
What is the question of nullification when sins and obedience are equal? The passage sets up the issue.
2
Understand the balance mechanism
Notice that the outweighing side nullifies an equal amount from itself and the outweighed, leaving a surplus.
3
See how it avoids arbitrary preference
The key is that the nullification is proportional, so no side is arbitrarily favored.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أبو هاشم بل يوازن بين طاعاته ومعاصيه فأيهما رجح أحبط الآخر وينحبط من الراجح أيضاً ما يساوي مقدار المرجوح ويبقى الزائد فيكون الراجح حينئذ قد أحبط المرجوح على هذا الوجه الذي لا يستلزم ترجيح أحد المتساويين على الآخر، ( ولما أبطلنا الأصل ) الذي هو استحقاق العقاب والثواب بالمعصية والطاعة ( بطل الفرع ) المبني عليه وهو الإحباط مطلقاً سواء كان بطريق الموازنة أو غيرها ) ثم نقول لهم أي للبهشمية: كل واحد من الاستحقاقين المتساويين لو أبطل الآخر فإما معاً فيكون الشيء موجوداً حال كونه معدوماً لأن وجود كل منهما يقارن عدم الآخر فيلزم عدمهما معاً حال وجودهما معاً أو لا معاً بل ينعدم أحدهما فيبطل الآخر ثم يكر الآخر عليه فيغلبه، وأنه باطل لأنه لما كان قاصراً عن الغلبة قبل حتى صار مغلوباً فكيف لا يكون قاصراً عنها إذا صدر مغلوباً، وقد يجاب بأن كل واحد من العلمين يؤثر الاستحقاق الناشئ من الآخر حتى يبقى من أحد الاستحقاقين بقية بحسب رجحانه فليس الكاسر والمنكسر واحداً كما لم يتحدا في المزاج أيضاً
And Abu Hashim said: Rather, one weighs between his acts of obedience and his sins, and whichever of them outweighs nullifies the other, and from the outweighing one also is nullified what equals the amount of the outweighed, and the surplus remains. So the outweighing one at that time has nullified the outweighed in this manner, which does not entail preferring one of the two equals over the other. (And since we have nullified the principle) which is the deservingness of punishment and reward by disobedience and obedience, (the branch) built upon it is nullified, which is nullification absolutely, whether by way of balance or otherwise. Then we say to them, i.e., to the Bahshamiyya: Each one of the two deserts (equal) if it nullifies the other, then either both together, then the thing would exist while being non-existent because the existence of each is concomitant with the non-existence of the other, so their non-existence would be necessitated together while they exist together; or not together, rather one becomes non-existent, then the other nullifies it, then the other repeats upon it and overcomes it. And that is invalid, because since it was incapable of overcoming before, such that it became overcome, how would it not be incapable of it when it emerges overcome? And it may be answered: Each one of the two knowledges influences the desert arising from the other, until a remainder from one of the two deserts remains according to its preponderance, so the breaker and the broken are not one, just as they are not united in the mixture also.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage presents Abu Hashim's view of balance (muwāzana) between acts of obedience and sins. He proposes that the preponderant side nullifies the other, and from the preponderant an amount equal to the outweighed is also nullified, leaving a surplus. This avoids arbitrarily favoring one equal over another. The passage then refutes the principle of deservingness (istiḥqāq) upon which nullification is based, thereby invalidating the whole doctrine of nullification. An objection is raised: if two equal deserts try to nullify each other, either they cancel simultaneously (impossible, as something cannot exist and not exist at once) or one nullifies the other and then the other overcomes it (impossible, as the weaker cannot later become stronger). The answer to this objection is that each desert influences the other, so a remainder is left in the preponderant one. Thus the 'breaking' and 'broken' are not the same entity, avoiding the contradiction.

Key Terms
موازنة
استحقاق
إحباط
راجح
مرجوح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Balance requires arbitrarily choosing one side when they are equal.
Correction: Abu Hashim's balance nullifies an equal amount from both sides, leaving the surplus of the preponderant, so no arbitrary choice is made.

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hashim's balance view, what happens to the preponderant side when it nullifies the outweighed?
A) It is completely nullified.
B) It nullifies an amount equal to the outweighed from itself and keeps the surplus.
C) It remains unaffected.
D) It nullifies the outweighed but loses nothing.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hashim's balance preserves logical consistency by proportional nullification, leaving a surplus from the preponderant side.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine your own scale of good and bad deeds, which side do you truly believe outweighs? What does that tell you about your current state with Allah?
?
Abu Hashim’s model says that even if your good deeds outweigh, a portion equal to your bad deeds is still nullified. How does this make you feel about the bad deeds you have committed today—are you content to let them be balanced out, or are they weighing on your heart?
?
The ‘surplus’ that remains after balancing is what you will meet Allah with. Are you actively increasing that surplus through sincere actions, or are you hoping that your good deeds will simply cancel your bad ones without any extra effort?

Refuting the Principle and the Objection of Mutual Nullification
Refutation of principle and objection to Bahshamiyya with answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection to the Bahshamiyya regarding mutual nullification of equal deserts, and the answer that each desert influences the other to leave a remainder.

Core Idea
Mutual nullification leads to contradiction; the answer is that influence leaves a remainder.

Having refuted the principle of deservingness (istiḥqāq) outright, the author presents a specific objection against the Bahshamiyya: if two equal deserts try to nullify each other, absurdities arise. The answer explains that each desert influences the other, preserving a remainder for the preponderant.

Guided Path
1
Understand the refutation of the principle
The author says since the principle of reward/punishment based on acts is nullified, the branch (nullification) is also nullified.
2
Analyze the objection
Consider the two options if equal deserts nullify each other: simultaneously (impossible) or sequentially (problematic because the weaker cannot later become stronger).
3
Explore the answer
Each desert influences the other, leaving a remainder in the preponderant, thus avoiding the contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Misconception: The objection proves that nullification is impossible in all cases.

What is the problem with the sequential nullification of two equal deserts according to the objection?
A) It violates causality.
B) The weaker desert cannot later overcome after being overcome.
C) It leads to infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever comfort yourself by thinking that your good deeds cancel out the bad, as if the scales are balanced? This lesson exposes the logical problem with complete nullification. How does the idea that every sin leaves a 'remainder' change the way you view repentance? Will you seek forgiveness for each sin individually, rather than assuming one good deed erases many?
?
The objection argues that simultaneous nullification leads to contradiction—a thing cannot both exist and not exist. In your spiritual life, do you sometimes live in contradiction, believing you can please God while clinging to a pet sin? How does this passage's insistence on logical consistency call you to examine your own consistency in faith and action?
?
The answer in the passage speaks of influence leaving a remainder according to preponderance. This means that the weight of your deeds matters—every action leaves a trace. Are you aware that your small, hidden sins accumulate, but also that your good deeds, even if small, leave a lasting mark? What does this teach you about the seriousness of every moment of your life? How will you live differently today, knowing that nothing is ever completely lost or completely erased?

The Mu'tazilites' Claim and the Reply: Reward and Punishment Cannot Be Equal
Appendix on Mu'tazilite agreement and the Sunni reply.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite argument that reward and punishment cannot be equal, the disagreement between al-Jubba'i and Abu Hashim on its basis, and the Sunni reply that divine favor and the tenfold reward override any supposed equality.

Core Idea
Even if deeds are equal, mercy outweighs justice.

This appendix addresses a key Mu'tazilite claim: that reward and punishment cannot be equal, because if they were, they would cancel out, leaving the responsible person without any outcome. The passage presents internal disagreements among the Mu'tazilites on the rational basis of this impossibility, and then offers a Sunni reply based on the preponderance of reward and God's grace.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic without analysis, then read the translation to understand the flow. Notice the word 'تذنيب' indicates an appendix.
2
Identify the two parts
The passage first states the Mu'tazilite agreement, then gives a reply starting with 'والجواب'.
3
Examine the internal Mu'tazilite disagreement
Note that al-Jubba'i says impossibility is rational, while Abu Hashim says it is by consensus.
4
Analyze the reply arguments
The reply uses two arguments: the tenfold reward for good deeds and the possibility of divine favor granting reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تذنيب . قد اتفق المعتزلة أي الجبائيان وأتباعهما على أنه لا يتساوى الثواب والعقاب أي لا يتساوى الطاعات والزلات وإلا تساقطا إذ لا يجوز بقاؤهما معاً لما مر من التنافي بين الثواب والعقاب وبين استحقاقيهما أيضاً ولا يجوز إسقاط أحدهما بالآخر لتساويهما فرضاً، وإذا تساقطا معاً فلا يكون ثمة ثواب ولا عقاب وإنه محال فعند الجبائي عقلاً لأن إبطال كل منهما للآخر إما معاً أو على التعاقب وكلاهما محال لما عرفت وعند أبي هاشم إِن العقل لا يدل على امتناع التساوي إذ ما من مرتبة من مراتب الطاعات إلا ويجوز العقل بلوغ المعاصي إليها وبالعكس ولا استحالة العقل في تساقطهما أيضاً لأن كل واحد من العملين يؤثر في استحقاق الآخر كما مر إنما استحالته للإجماع على أن لا خروج للمكلف عنهما بل كل مكلف إما من أهل الجنة أو النار ، ولا بد له من الخلود في أحدهما ولا يتصور وقوع أحد الخلودين من جهة أن مع التساوي في الموجب وإنما فسرنا المعتزلة بالجبائيين وأتباعهما لما سلف من جمهورهم ذهبوا إلى إحباط جميع الطاعات بمعصية واحدة وحينئذ فإحباط المعصية للطاعة المساوية لها يكون عندهم أولى . والجواب : لم لا يجوز على تقدير تساوي الطاعات والمعاصي أن يثاب لما مر من جانب الثواب أرجح فإن الحسنة تجزى بعشر أمثالها والسيئة لا تجزى إلا بمثلها، وأيضاً على تقدير التساوي والتساقط معاً لا يلزم خلو المكلف عن الثواب والعقاب لجواز التفضل بالثواب عندنا
Appendix. The Mu'tazila, i.e., al-Jubba'iyan and their followers, have agreed that reward and punishment cannot be equal, i.e., acts of obedience and slips cannot be equal; otherwise they would cancel each other, since it is not permissible for both to remain together, due to what has passed of the mutual contradiction between reward and punishment and between their deserts, and it is not permissible to drop one by the other due to their equalness by assumption. And if they cancel each other together, then there would be no reward and no punishment, and that is impossible. According to al-Jubba'i, it is impossible rationally, because the nullification of each by the other is either together or successively, and both are impossible for what you have known. And according to Abu Hashim, reason does not indicate the impossibility of equality, since there is no rank among the ranks of acts of obedience except that reason permits wills to reach it, and vice versa, and there is no rational impossibility in their mutual cancellation either, because each one of the deeds influences the desert of the other, as passed. Its impossibility is only due to the consensus that there is no exit for the responsible person from them both. Rather, every responsible person is either among the people of Paradise or the Fire, and he must be immortal in one of them, and it is inconceivable that one of the two immortalities occurs from the perspective that with equality in the cause. And we only interpreted the Mu'tazila as al-Jubba'iyan and their followers because of what preceded that the majority of them went to the nullification of all acts of obedience by a single sin, and in that case the nullification of the sin for the act of obedience equal to it is more appropriate according to them. And the answer: Why is it not permissible, on the assumption of equality of acts of obedience and sins, that he be rewarded, due to what has passed that the side of reward is more preponderant, for a good deed is rewarded tenfold and an evil deed is only recompensed with its like? And also, on the assumption of equality and mutual cancellation together, the responsible person being free from reward and punishment is not necessitated, because it is permissible for [God] to bestow favor with reward according to us.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This appendix (tadhnīb) states that the Mu'tazilites (al-Jubba'iyan and followers) agree that reward and punishment cannot be equal, because if equal they would cancel out, which is impossible. For al-Jubba'i, this impossibility is rational: nullification of each by the other either simultaneously or successively is absurd. For Abu Hashim, reason does not forbid equality; it is impossible only by consensus, since every responsible person must end up in Paradise or Hell. The passage then clarifies who is meant by 'Mu'tazila' here. Finally, a reply is given: even if acts of obedience and sins are equal and cancel out, one can still be rewarded because good deeds are rewarded tenfold (so reward outweighs punishment), and God may also grant reward by pure favor (tafaḍḍul). Thus the responsible person is not left without reward or punishment.

Key Terms
تساوي
ثواب
عقاب
تفضل
إجماع
خلود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the impossibility of equal reward and punishment is purely rational for all Mu'tazilites.
Correction: Abu Hashim holds that reason does not forbid equality; it is only impossible by consensus (ijmāʿ).

Checkpoint
Why does Abu Hashim consider the impossibility of equal reward and punishment to be based on consensus rather than reason?
A) Because reason cannot prove the existence of reward.
B) Because reason permits in principle that acts could be equal in rank.
C) Because reason demands that every person must be rewarded or punished.
D) Because consensus is more reliable than reason.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite argument collapses because divine grace and the tenfold reward ensure that reward is not dependent on exact equality of deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own deeds, do you rely more on the scale of justice or the hope of God's multiplication of good deeds? Which mindset truly dominates your heart in moments of weakness?
?
If God were to treat your good and bad deeds as exactly equal, would you be content with that justice, or would you despair? What does your honest answer reveal about your reliance on His mercy?
?
The lesson shows that even if deeds cancel out, God may still reward by tafaḍḍul. Are you living today as if you actually expect that generosity, or do you harbor a hidden belief that you must earn His favor? How would your actions change if you fully believed in tafaḍḍul?

Al-Jurjani's Critique of Mu'tazilite Position on Minor Sins
Al-Jurjani scrutinizes Mu'tazilite view on minor sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Jurjani refines the Mu'tazilite position on deserving punishment for minor sins, distinguishing between pure minor sins and those accompanied by major sins.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazilites may deny any deserved punishment for minor sins, contrary to common understanding.

In this gloss, Al-Jurjani examines the Mu'tazilite claim that they do not affirm deserved punishment for minor sins in a certain non-disputed case. He suggests that their position might actually be that there is no deserved punishment for pure minor sins, while for minor sins with major sins they allow possibility of forgiveness. He further argues that their denial of intercession shows they reject deserved punishment for minor sins absolutely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how Al-Jurjani begins by referencing a previous statement and then probes the Mu'tazilite view.
Pay attention to the distinction between pure minor sins and those with major sins.
2
Identify the two interpretations
The passage presents two possible understandings of the Mu'tazilite position. Find them and note how each is supported.
3
Understand the intercession argument
Al-Jurjani uses the Mu'tazilite denial of intercession to argue that they deny deserved punishment for all minor sins. Reflect on this connection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولا يقولون به في غير صورة النزاع فيه بحث إذ لعلهم يقولون لا استحقاق بالصغائر الصرفة كما يدل عليه استدلالهم بقوله تعالى : وإن تجتنبوا كبائر ما تنهون عنه نكفر عنكم سيئاتكم ﴾ [النساء : ٣١] ، وأما الصغائر المقرونة بالكبائر ففيها الاستحقاق عندهم أيضاً، فيجوز أن يعفو الله تعالى عنها ويمكن أن يقال : لم يثبت منهم القول باستحقاق العقاب بارتكاب الصغيرة أصلاً، وإن أوهم به في الجملة استدلالهم على نفيه بالآية الكريمة ويدل على إنكارهم استحقاق العقاب بها مطلقاً إنكارهم الشفاعة لدرء العقاب كما لا يخفى على المنصف
His saying: (And they do not affirm it in the non-disputed case) there is investigation in it, for perhaps they say there is no deserving for pure minor sins, as indicated by their argument with His saying: 'If you avoid the major sins that you are forbidden, We will expiate for you your minor sins' [4:31]. As for minor sins accompanied by major sins, there is deserving according to them as well, so God may forgive them. And it can be said: that the statement affirming deserving of punishment for committing a minor sin has not been established from them at all, even if their argument for its negation with the noble verse gives that impression. And their denial of intercession to ward off punishment indicates their denial of deserving punishment for them absolutely, as is not hidden from the fair-minded.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This is a critical gloss on the first proof of the previous section. The commentator scrutinizes the claim that the Mu'tazilites do not affirm deserved punishment for minor sins in the non-disputed case. He suggests that perhaps they do say there is no deserved punishment for pure minor sins (not accompanied by major sins), as their use of Quran 4:31 indicates. For minor sins accompanied by major sins, they do hold deserving, but God may forgive. He further argues that it has not been proven that the Mu'tazilites affirm deserved punishment for any minor sin at all; their denial of intercession (to avert punishment) shows they deny absolute deserving of punishment for minor sins. The passage thus refines the understanding of the Mu'tazilite position.

Key Terms
صغائر صرفة (sagha'ir sifah)
استحقاق (istihqaq)
شفاعة (shafa'ah)
عفو ('afw)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Mu'tazilites affirm deserved punishment for all minor sins.
Correction: Al-Jurjani shows they may deny it for pure minor sins, and perhaps even for all minor sins, as indicated by their denial of intercession.

Checkpoint
According to the gloss, what does the Mu'tazilite denial of intercession indicate?
A) They affirm deserved punishment for major sins only.
B) They deny deserved punishment for pure minor sins but affirm for those with major sins.
C) They deny deserved punishment for all minor sins absolutely.
D) They allow intercession for minor sins.

Key Takeaway
Al-Jurjani argues that the Mu'tazilites likely deny any deserved punishment for minor sins, contrary to initial impressions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a 'minor' sin (like a lie or backbiting), do you feel it matters little, or do you treat it as seriously as a major sin? How does Al-Jurjani's analysis of the Mu'tazilite position challenge your own complacency about small sins?
?
The Mu'tazilites argued that God must punish sin or justice is violated. Do you ever feel entitled to God's forgiveness without sincere repentance, assuming sin is 'no big deal'? What would it mean for you to take even minor sins seriously as acts deserving of divine attention?
?
Al-Jurjani points out that denying intercession implies denying any deserved punishment. If you truly believed every minor sin could be punished, would you change any habit today? What is one specific minor sin you will consciously avoid this week as a result of this lesson?

Major and Minor Sins and the Origin of Excommunication
Defines major and minor sins and names the first proponents of excommunication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between major and minor sins and who first introduced the concept that major sins expel one from faith.

Core Idea
The first theologians to claim major sins expel from faith were Wāṣil b. ‘Aṭā’ and ‘Amr b. ‘Ubayd.

This passage from al-Mawaqif introduces two categories of sin—major and minor—and clarifies that committing a major sin does not expel one from faith entirely, but renders one sinful. It also traces the origin of the view that major sins expel to the founders of the Mu‘tazila.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how the author defines both major and minor sins and inserts a historical note.
The passage is concise but packed with definitions and a historical reference.
2
Identify the two categories and their effects
Find the definitions of major sins (كبائر) and minor sins (صغائر). Notice what each category does to the sinner's status: major sins expel to sinfulness (فسق), minor sins do not expel.
The examples given are important: murder, transgression, fornication, wine for major; uncovering private parts, foolishness for minor.
3
Recognize the historical origin
The passage states that the first to originate the view of excommunication were Wāṣil b. ‘Aṭā’ and ‘Amr b. ‘Ubayd. Note that they are the founders of the Mu‘tazila school.
This counters the Khawarij view that all sins expel from faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثالث - المقصد الثالث : في الكفر بالإيمان لإيهامه عدم التصديق بل يحكم عليه بالفسق ( ويعبر عنهما ) أي عن المعاصي المخرجة إلى تلك المنزلة بالكبائر) كالقتل العمد والعدوان والزنا وشرب الخمر ونظائرهما وأول من أحدث القول بهذا الإخراج واصل بن عطاء وعمرو بن عبيد، ( ومنها ما لا يخرج أي قسم لا يخرج ) ككشف العورة والسفه، ويسمى بالصغائر ولا يوصف صاحبها بالكفر ولا بالفسق بل بالإيمان ) وسنزيده ) أي نزيد ما ذكرناه في هذا المقصد من قول الخوارج والمعتزلة ( بياناً في المقصد الذي يتلوه.
The third observatory - the third objective: On disbelief by [؟] faith because it suggests non-belief, rather he is judged to be sinful. And they are expressed by them, i.e., the sins that expel to that station as major sins, like intentional murder and transgression, fornication, drinking wine, and their likes. And the first to originate the statement of this expulsion was Wāṣil b. ‘Aṭā’ and ‘Amr b. ‘Ubayd. And among them are those that do not expel, meaning a category that does not expel, like uncovering the private parts and foolishness, and they are called minor sins, and their doer is not described with disbelief nor with sinfulness but with faith. And we will increase it, i.e., we increase what we mentioned in this objective from the statement of the Khawarij and the Mu‘tazila, with clarification in the objective that follows it.

Commentary
This passage defines the two categories of sins – major and minor – and states that the first to speak of the view that major sins expel one from faith were Wāṣil b. ‘Aṭā’ and ‘Amr b. ‘Ubayd, the founders of the Mu‘tazila. It begins by clarifying that a person who commits a sin that suggests disbelief is judged to be sinful, not a disbeliever. The terms ‘major sins’ are used for sins that expel to the station of sinfulness, while ‘minor sins’ are those that do not expel, such as uncovering private parts or foolishness. The doer of a minor sin is described as a believer, not a disbeliever or sinful. The passage ends by promising further clarification in the following objective.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between major and minor sins hinges on whether they expel from the state of faith to sinfulness, and this view originated with the Mu‘tazila.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Mu'tazila taught that a person who commits a major sin is a fāsiq, not a kāfir. Have you ever considered someone who committed a grave sin as having lost their faith? How should this passage change how you view and treat Muslims who fall into major sins? Will you commit to not excommunicating them in your heart?
?
The originators of the view that sins expel used rational argument (ʿaql) to establish a middle ground. But where does your own intellect lead you when you reason about Allah's judgment? Do you trust revelation more than your reasoning? Pause now and ask Allah to keep you from innovating in matters of faith.

The Fourth Objective: Three Positions on the Major Sinner
Al-Jurjani states the maqsad and three positions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three historical positions regarding the status of a Muslim who commits a major sin.

Core Idea
The major sinner is a believer according to Ahl al-Sunna.

In this section, al-Jurjani introduces the fourth objective of the third observation: the ruling on the committer of a major sin from among the people of the qibla. He notes that earlier discussions on the reality of faith are relevant, and his aim is to present the opposing views and then answer their doubts. Let's first see what those opposing views are.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once to understand the setting and the three positions. Then read the translation.
Notice that the author references a previous discussion on the reality of faith.
2
Identify the three positions
List the three groups mentioned: Khawarij, al-Hasan al-Basri, and Mu'tazila. Note their respective rulings on the major sinner.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this issue is important in Islamic theology and how each position affects the unity of the Muslim community.
This lesson sets the stage for the proofs and rebuttals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الرابع: في أن مرتكب الكبيرة من أهل الصلاة ] ) في أن مرتكب الكبيرة من أهل الصلاة أي من أهل القبلة ( مؤمن، وقد تقدم في مسألة حقيقة الإيمان، وغرضنا هاهنا ذكر مذهب المخالفين. والجواب عن شبهتهم : ذهب الخوارج إلى أنه كافر والحسن البصري إلى أنه منافق، والمعتزلة إلى أنه لا مؤمن ولا كافر حجة الخارج وجوه : الأول : قوله تعالى : ومن لم يحكم بما أنزل الله فأولئك هم الكافرون ﴾ [المائدة : ٤٤] ، فإن كلمة من عامة في كل من لم يحكم بما أنزل فيدخل فيه الفاسق المصدق، وأيضاً فقد علل كفرهم بعدم الحكم فكل من لم يحكم بما أنزل الله كان كافراً، والفاسق لم يحكم بما أنزل الله (قلنا : ) الموصولات لم توضع للعموم بل هي للجنس تحتمل العموم والخصوص، فنقول : المراد من لم يحكم بشيء مما أنزل الله أصلاً) ولا نزاع في كونه كافراً ، ( أو ) نقول : المراد بما أنزل الله ) هو التوراة بقرينة ما قبله وهو إنا أنزلنا التوراة ﴾ [المائدة : ٤٤] الآية، وأمتنا غير متعبدين بالحكم فيختص باليهود فيلزم أن يكونوا كافرين إذا لم يحكموا بالتوراة، ونحن نقول بموجبه.
The fourth objective: concerning that the committer of a major sin from the people of prayer – i.e., from the people of the qibla – is a believer. This has already been discussed in the issue of the reality of faith. Our purpose here is to mention the position of the opponents and the response to their doubts. The Khawarij held that he is an unbeliever, al-Hasan al-Basri that he is a hypocrite, and the Mu'tazila that he is neither a believer nor an unbeliever. The proof of the Kharijite [consists of] aspects: The first: His statement, exalted is He, ‘And whoever does not judge by what Allah has revealed – then it is those who are the disbelievers’ (al-Ma'idah 5:44). For the word ‘whoever’ is general concerning everyone who does not judge by what He revealed, so it includes the sinful person who affirms [faith]. Also, He made their unbelief conditional upon not judging, so everyone who does not judge by what Allah revealed is an unbeliever, and the sinful person does not judge by what Allah revealed. We say: Relative pronouns were not placed for generality; rather they are for the genus, admitting both generality and particularity. So we say: The intended meaning is the one who does not judge by anything of what Allah revealed at all; there is no dispute that he is an unbeliever. Or we say: The intended meaning of ‘what Allah revealed’ is the Torah, by the context of what precedes it, namely ‘Indeed, We sent down the Torah’ (al-Ma'idah 5:44), and our community is not obligated to judge by it, so it is specific to the Jews, thus it follows that they are unbelievers when they do not judge by the Torah, and we affirm its implication.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage introduces the fourth objective of the third observation: the status of the person who commits a major sin among the people of the qibla. The matn states that such a person is a believer, referencing earlier discussion on the reality of faith, and announces the aim to present the opposing views and responses. The author recounts three positions: the Khawarij say he is an unbeliever (kafir), al-Hasan al-Basri says he is a hypocrite (munafiq), and the Mu'tazila say he is neither believer nor unbeliever. Then the first Khariji proof is given: the verse 'Whoever does not judge by what Allah revealed, those are the disbelievers.' The Kharijite argues that 'whoever' is general and includes the sinful Muslim, and because the verse conditions unbelief on not judging, the sinful person is an unbeliever. The response from the Ahl al-Sunna is twofold. First, relative pronouns (like 'whoever') are not inherently general; they are genus nouns that can be specified. So the verse means the one who does not judge by anything of Allah's revelation at all (i.e., the one who rejects all divine law), which is obviously unbelief. Second, by context, 'what Allah revealed' refers specifically to the Torah, as the preceding verse mentions sending down the Torah. Since Muslims are not obligated to judge by the Torah, the verse is exclusive to the Jews, and we affirm that they are unbelievers if they do not judge by it. Thus the proof is refuted.

Key Terms
الكبيرة
أهل الصلاة
الخوارج
الحسن البصري
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many Muslims think all offenders are simply believers or unbelievers without nuance.
Correction: This passage shows that different groups held distinct theological stances, not just two options.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of al-Hasan al-Basri on the major sinner?
A) He is an unbeliever
B) He is a hypocrite
C) He is neither a believer nor an unbeliever
D) He is a believer

Key Takeaway
The major sinner is a believer according to Ahl al-Sunna, but three opposing views exist from the Khawarij, al-Hasan al-Basri, and the Mu'tazila.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the three opposing positions—Khawarij (unbeliever), Hasan al-Basri (hypocrite), or Mu'tazila (neither)—have you ever felt in your heart toward a Muslim who fell into a major sin? Confess that judgment to Allah and commit to seeing them as a believer in need of help.
?
You now know that Ahl al-Sunna says the major sinner is still a believer. Does your treatment of sinful Muslims reflect that belief, or do you distance yourself from them as if they were not part of the community? What specific relationship will you mend today?
?
The lesson mentions that the Ahl al-Sunna position was 'already discussed in the issue of the reality of faith.' Have you truly internalized that your own salvation does not depend on your perfection, but on Allah's mercy and the reality of your faith? What sin are you holding onto that makes you doubt that you are still a believer despite it?

The First Khariji Proof from Qur'an 5:44
First Khariji proof from Qur'an 5:44 and its reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Khariji argument that the verse 'Whoever does not judge by what Allah revealed' proves that a major sinner is an unbeliever.

Core Idea
The Kharijites use a general Qur'anic verse to condemn all sinners.

The Khawarij, known for their extreme stance, present several proofs for declaring a major sinner an unbeliever. The first proof is based on a clear Qur'anic verse from Surah al-Ma'idah. Let's examine this argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof
Read the Arabic passage containing the Khariji argument. Note the verse and the logical steps they take.
The verse is Qur'an 5:44, a key text for this issue.
2
Analyze the reasoning
Identify two points: the generality of 'whoever' (man) and the conditional structure tying unbelief to not judging.
They argue that since 'whoever' is general, it includes sinful Muslims, and since they do not judge by divine law, they are unbelievers.
3
Consider the strength
Reflect on why this argument appears compelling at first glance and why it needs a response.
This will prepare you for the rebuttal in the next lesson.

The Refutation of the First Khariji Proof
Sunni rebuttal with two arguments: specification and contextual limitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two-part Sunni response that specifies the verse's meaning and contextual scope.

Core Idea
The verse is not general; it applies to total rejection or to the Jews.

Al-Jurjani now presents the Sunni response to the Khariji proof. He gives two arguments: one based on the nature of relative pronouns, and another based on the context of the verse. Together, they show that the verse does not apply to the sinful Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Read the response
Read the Arabic passage containing the rebuttal. Note that it begins with 'قلنا' (We say).
There are two distinct answers introduced by 'أو' (or) indicating alternative arguments.
2
Understand the first argument
The first argument focuses on the nature of relative pronouns (al-mawsūlāt). They are not inherently general; they can be specified. Therefore, 'whoever' can mean 'the one who completely rejects divine law'—which is unanimously unbelief.
This refutes the claim of absolute generality.
3
Understand the second argument
The second argument uses context: the preceding verse mentions the Torah, so 'what Allah revealed' refers specifically to the Torah. Jews are addressed; Muslims are not obligated to judge by it. Hence the verse is limited to the Jews.
This refutes the application to Muslims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الرابع: في أن مرتكب الكبيرة من أهل الصلاة ] ) في أن مرتكب الكبيرة من أهل الصلاة أي من أهل القبلة ( مؤمن، وقد تقدم في مسألة حقيقة الإيمان، وغرضنا هاهنا ذكر مذهب المخالفين. والجواب عن شبهتهم : ذهب الخوارج إلى أنه كافر والحسن البصري إلى أنه منافق، والمعتزلة إلى أنه لا مؤمن ولا كافر حجة الخارج وجوه : الأول : قوله تعالى : ومن لم يحكم بما أنزل الله فأولئك هم الكافرون ﴾ [المائدة : ٤٤] ، فإن كلمة من عامة في كل من لم يحكم بما أنزل فيدخل فيه الفاسق المصدق، وأيضاً فقد علل كفرهم بعدم الحكم فكل من لم يحكم بما أنزل الله كان كافراً، والفاسق لم يحكم بما أنزل الله (قلنا : ) الموصولات لم توضع للعموم بل هي للجنس تحتمل العموم والخصوص، فنقول : المراد من لم يحكم بشيء مما أنزل الله أصلاً) ولا نزاع في كونه كافراً ، ( أو ) نقول : المراد بما أنزل الله ) هو التوراة بقرينة ما قبله وهو إنا أنزلنا التوراة ﴾ [المائدة : ٤٤] الآية، وأمتنا غير متعبدين بالحكم فيختص باليهود فيلزم أن يكونوا كافرين إذا لم يحكموا بالتوراة، ونحن نقول بموجبه.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read this rebuttal against the Kharijis, do you see any tendency in your own heart to use isolated verses to condemn others without understanding their context? Write down a specific situation where you have done this, and commit to studying the context before making a judgment this week.
?
The first argument says the verse applies only to those who utterly reject divine revelation. Are there areas in your life where you only partially follow God's commands, thinking that is acceptable as long as you affirm faith? This lesson challenges that comfort. Choose one area where your obedience is incomplete and make a concrete plan to submit fully.
?
The second argument makes the verse specific to the Jews. How often do you apply harsh verses to others when they are actually directed at a different people or situation? Ask Allah for humility and wisdom to apply scripture correctly, and practice self-accountability before pointing fingers.

The Khawarij and Hasan al-Basri on the Major Sinner
Al-Jurjani explains the Khawarij and Hasan al-Basri positions with analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Khawarij and Hasan al-Basri positions on the major sinner and how the commentator reduces Hasan's position to that of the Khawarij.

Core Idea
Hasan al-Basri's 'hypocrite' position ultimately implies unbelief unless it means weak faith.

In this passage, al-Jurjani explains the positions of the Khawarij and Hasan al-Basri regarding the status of the major sinner. He also analyzes Hasan's position, showing that it aligns with the Khawarij unless reinterpreted as mere weakness of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the three positions
Read the first part of the Arabic passage that describes the Khawarij, Azariqa, and Hasan al-Basri positions. Note the specific terms used: 'kafir', 'mushrik', 'munafiq'.
The Azariqa are a sub-sect of the Khawarij.
2
Understand the linguistic origin of 'munafiq'
The commentary explains the word 'munafiq' comes from a jerboa's burrow. See how this metaphor illustrates hiding unbelief.
3
Reflect on the commentator's analysis
The commentator argues that Hasan's position essentially means the major sinner is an unbeliever. Consider why he says this, and what the alternative interpretation of 'weak faith' would mean.
This connects to the learning objective about understanding the doctrinal alignment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ذهب الخوارج إلى أنه (كافر وذهب الأزارقة إلى أنه مشترك لأنه يعمل عملاً لله تعالى، وعملاً لغيره وهو نفسه أو الشيطان أو غيرهما. قوله : ( والحسن البصري إلى أنه (منافق أي مظهر للإيمان مبطن للكفر، وأصله من نافق اليربوع أي أخذ في نافقائه وهي إحدى جحريه يكتمها ويظهر غيرها، وهو موضع يرفعه، فإذا أتى من قبل القاصعاء وهو جحره الذي يقصع فيه أي يدخل ضرب النافقاء برأسه فينفق ويخرج منه، والحق أن مذهب الحسن راجع إلى مذهب الخوارج ولا يمكن حمل كلامه على أنه مؤمن في الجملة وإن لم يكن مؤمناً كاملاً، لأن الوجه الثاني من وجهي استدلاله على مذهبه يدل على عدم الاعتقاد فيكون كافراً، اللهم إلا أن يراد بنفي الاعتقاد تضعيفه على نمط قولهم : زيد ليس بشيء وعلى هذا يؤول إلى كلام أهل السنة والمشهور خلافه وفي بعض الكتب أن الحسن البصري رجع عن هذا المذهب.
قوله : (المراد من لم يحكم بشيء مما أنزل الله تعالى أصلاً) وقد يجاب بأن الحكم بالشيء التصديق به، ولا شك أن من لم يصدق بما أنزل الله تعالى فهو كافر، وليس بشيء لأن السياق صريح في أن المراد بالحكم بما أنزل الله تعالى هو القضاء فيما بين الناس بما يوافقه لا معناه الاصطلاحي الذي هو التصديق.
His statement: 'The Khawarij held that he is an unbeliever, and the Azariqa held that he is a polytheist because he performs an act for Allah and an act for other than Him – that is, himself or Satan or others.' His statement: 'And al-Hasan al-Basri held that he is a hypocrite' – that is, one who outwardly shows faith and inwardly conceals unbelief. Its origin is from the jerboa's 'nafiqa' – that is, it enters its 'nafiqa', which is one of its two burrows; it hides it and shows the other, and it is a place it lifts up. When it comes from the side of the 'qasi'a', which is its burrow where it enters, it strikes the 'nafiqa' with its head, then it emerges from it. The truth is that the position of al-Hasan reverts to the position of the Khawarij, and his speech cannot be interpreted as meaning that he is a believer in a general sense even if not a perfect believer, because the second of the two aspects of his inference for his position indicates the absence of belief, so he would be an unbeliever – unless what is meant by negation of belief is its weakness in the manner of their saying 'Zayd is nothing'. On this, it returns to the speech of Ahl al-Sunna, but the well-known view is contrary, and in some books it is mentioned that al-Hasan al-Basri retracted this position. His statement: 'The intended meaning is the one who does not judge by anything of what Allah revealed at all' – and it may also be answered that judgment concerning a thing is affirmation of it, and there is no doubt that whoever does not affirm what Allah revealed is an unbeliever. But it is nothing because the context is explicit that the intended meaning of 'judgment by what Allah revealed' is adjudication among people in accordance with it, not its technical meaning which is affirmation.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is a commentary note from the sharh. It first explains the Khariji position in more detail, mentioning that the Azariqa (a sub-sect of Khawarij) consider the major sinner a polytheist (mushrik) because he mixes an act for Allah with an act for himself or Satan. Then it explains al-Hasan al-Basri's position that he is a hypocrite, providing a linguistic derivation from the jerboa's burrow to illustrate the idea of hiding unbelief. The commentator asserts that al-Hasan's position actually reduces to that of the Khawarij, because one of the two aspects of his inference indicates absence of faith, implying unbelief. However, it is possible that by 'negation of faith' he meant weakness of faith, which aligns with Ahl al-Sunna, but the well-known view is that he held a different opinion, and some books claim he retracted. The second part of the passage addresses the phrase from the earlier response: 'The intended meaning is the one who does not judge by anything of what Allah revealed at all.' An additional response is given: the word 'judgment' (hukm) can mean 'affirmation' (tasdiq), so the verse would mean 'whoever does not affirm what Allah revealed' – and that is unbelief. However, this interpretation is rejected because the context clearly indicates that 'judgment' here refers to adjudication among people, not the technical term of affirmation. Thus this alternative answer is not valid.

Key Terms
الأزارقة
المنافق
النافقاء
القاصعاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Hasan al-Basri's position of 'hypocrite' is distinct from unbelief and does not imply kufr.
Correction: The commentator shows that his position equates to unbelief because one of his inferences indicates absence of belief, unless reinterpreted as weak faith.

Checkpoint
What does the commentator say about the position of al-Hasan al-Basri on the major sinner?
A) He holds that the major sinner is a believer with weak faith
B) His position is essentially the same as the Khawarij's, implying unbelief
C) He holds that the major sinner is a hypocrite who is still a believer
D) He agrees with the Mu'tazila

Key Takeaway
Hasan al-Basri's description of the major sinner as a hypocrite is seen by the commentator as equivalent to unbelief, aligning with the Khawarij, unless it refers to weak faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a Muslim committing a major sin, do you ever feel a sense of superiority or assume your own faith is stronger? How does the Khawarij's extreme view warn you against self-righteousness in your own heart?
?
The commentator argues that Hasan al-Basri's label of 'hypocrite' effectively means unbelief. Are there people in your life you have secretly labelled as 'hypocrites'? On what basis? How does this lesson challenge you to examine your own heart rather than passing judgment?
?
The linguistic analogy from the jerboa burrow illustrates hiding one thing while showing another. In what area of your life are you most tempted to 'burrow' and hide your true state from others? What would it cost you to be honest with Allah and with those around you?

The Second Response: Interpreting Hukm in the Verse
Al-Jurjani presents and rejects an alternative interpretation of 'hukm' in the verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second response to the first proof regarding the interpretation of 'hukm' in the verse and why it is rejected.

Core Idea
The verse's 'hukm' means adjudication, not affirmation; thus the alternative tasdiq interpretation fails.

In this short passage, al-Jurjani presents an alternative answer to the earlier response. Some might argue that 'hukm' means 'tasdiq' (affirmation), so whoever does not affirm is a kafir. But the commentator rejects this because the context clearly refers to adjudication among people.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the intended meaning
Read the Arabic passage that begins with 'المراد من لم يحكم...' and its translation. Note the two possible meanings of 'hukm' mentioned.
2
Understand the proposed answer
Some could argue that 'hukm' here means 'tasdiq' (affirmation), so the verse would mean 'whoever does not affirm is an unbeliever.' Understand why this might be suggested.
This is an attempt to give a different interpretation.
3
Why the answer is rejected
The commentator rejects this because the context of the verse (in Surat al-Ma'ida) is about adjudicating disputes, not about belief. So 'hukm' cannot mean 'tasdiq' here.
This shows the importance of contextual interpretation.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Soundness of Islam Does Not Depend on Disputed Details
Author states principle and supports with historical evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the validity of a Muslim's faith is not contingent upon correct belief in every disputed theological detail.

Core Idea
Islam's validity rests on fundamentals, not on disputed details.

In this passage, the author establishes a critical principle in Islamic theology: that the soundness of one's Islam is not harmed by holding incorrect views on non-fundamental matters. He supports this by noting that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not demand detailed knowledge from his companions, implying that such knowledge is not a requirement for faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening principle
Read the first part where the author states that no one of ahl al-qibla is declared a disbeliever and that Islam's soundness is independent of knowledge of disputed matters.
2
Reflect on the conditional argument
Notice the 'if... then...' structure: if soundness depended on details, the Prophet would have investigated; but he did not, so it does not.
This is a powerful logical proof from the Prophet's practice.
3
Connect to your own understanding
Consider how this principle applies to common theological debates today. Does being mistaken on a non-essential point make one less of a Muslim?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثالث - المقصد الخامس : الاتفاق على أنه لا يكفر أحد من أهل القبلة تلك صحة دين الإسلام لا تتوقف على معرفة الحق في تلك المسائل و ( أن الخطأ فيها ليس قادحاً في حقيقة الإسلام إذا لو توقفت عليها وكان الخطأ قادحاً في الحقيقة لوجب أن يبحث عن كيفية اعتقادهم فيها، لكن لم يجر حديث شيء منها في زمانه عليه السلام ولا في زمانهم أصلاً ) فإن قيل : لعله عليه السلام عرف منهم ذلك ) أي كونهم عالمين بها إجمالا ) فلم يبحث عنها ) لذلك ) كما لم يبحث عن علمهم بعلمه وقدرته مع وجوب اعتقادهما)، وما ذلك إلا لعلمه بأنهم عالمون على طريق الجملة بأنه تعالى عالم ،قادر، فكذا الحال في تلك المسائل (قلنا :) ما ذكرتموه ) مكابرة ) لأنا نعلم أن الأعراب الذين جاؤوا إليه عليه السلام ما كانوا كلهم عالمين بأنه تعالى عالم بالعلم لا بالذات، وأنه مرئي في الدار الآخرة وأنه ليس بجسم ولا مكان وجهة وأنه قادر على أفعال بها ) أي بالنبوة ( دليلاً للعلم بها ، ولو إجمالاً فلذلك لم يبحث عنهما، قال الإمام الرازي: الأصول التي يتوقف عليها صحة نبوة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم أدلتها على ما يليق بأصحاب الجمل ظاهرة فإن من دخل بستاناً ورأى أزهاراً حادثة بعد أن لم تكن ثم رأى عنقود عنب قد اسود جميع حباته إلا حبة واحدة مع تساوي نسبة الماء والهواء وحر الشمس إلى جميع تلك الحبات فإنه يضطر إلى العلم بأن محدثه فاعل مختار لأن دلالة الفعل المحكم على علم فاعله واختياره ضرورية ودلالة المعجزة على صدق المدعى ضرورية أيضاً وإذا عرف هذه الأصول أمكن العلم بصدق الرسول فثبت أن أصول الإسلام جلية وأن أدلتها مجملة واضحة فلذلك لم يبحث عنها بخلاف المسائل التي اختلف فيها فإنها في الظهور والجلاء ليست مثل تلك الأصول بل أكثرها مما ورد في الكتاب والسنة ما يتخيله المبطل معارضاً لما يحتج به المحق فيها، وكل واحد منهما يدعي أن التأويل المطابق لمذهبه أولى فلا يمكن جعلها مما يتوقف عليه صحة الإسلام فلا يجوز الإقدام على التكفير إذ فيه خطر عظيم . إلى بيان الحق في التفاصيل عند ملاحظتها وإن كانت مما لا خلاف في تكفير المخالف فيها كحدوث العالم، فكم من مؤمن لم يعرف معنى الحادث والقديم أصلا ولم يخطر بباله حديث حشر الأجساد ،قطعاً، لكن إذا لاحظ ذلك فلو لم يصدق كان كافراً. والجواب : إنا نقطع بأن منهم من وقف على التفاصيل وإن لم يكن كلهم كذلك . قوله : ( بأصحاب الجمل ) أي أرباب الإجمال فإنهم لا يقدرون على تنقيح الدليل
The third observation - the fifth aim: Agreement that no one of the people of the qibla is declared a disbeliever. That. The soundness of the religion of Islam does not depend on knowing the truth in those matters, and (that error in them is not a defect in the reality of Islam, because if it depended on them and error were a defect in the reality, then it would be necessary to investigate the nature of their belief in them, but no mention of any of them occurred in his time, peace be upon him, nor in their time at all.) If it is said: Perhaps he, peace be upon him, knew from them that (i.e., that they knew them in summary) so he did not investigate them (for that reason) just as he did not investigate their knowledge of His knowledge and power despite the obligation of believing in them, and that is only because he knew that they know in a summary way that He, exalted, is knowing, powerful, so the case is the same in those matters. (We say:) What you mentioned is stubborn denial, because we know that the Bedouins who came to him, peace be upon him, were not all knowing that He, exalted, is knowing through knowledge not by essence, and that He is visible in the hereafter, and that He is not a body, nor place, nor direction, and that He is powerful over all the actions of servants, and that He is the creator of them entirely. So the claim that they knew them is known to be false necessarily. And (as for) knowledge and power, they are (among what the establishment of his prophethood depends on, because the indication of the miracle depends on them), so acknowledgment (and knowledge) of them (i.e., of prophethood) is a proof of knowledge of them, even if in summary. Therefore he did not investigate them. Imam al-Razi said: The principles on which the soundness of the prophethood of Muhammad, peace be upon him, depends—their proofs are apparent in a manner befitting the people of summary. For whoever enters a garden and sees flowers newly originated after not being, then sees a cluster of grapes whose all grapes have blackened except one grape, despite the equal proportion of water, air, and sun heat to all those grapes, he is compelled to know that its originator is a free agent, because the indication of the precise action to the knowledge and choice of its agent is necessary, and the indication of the miracle to the truthfulness of the claimant is also necessary. When these principles are known, knowledge of the truthfulness of the messenger is possible. So it is established that the principles of Islam are clear and their proofs are summary and clear. Therefore he did not investigate them, unlike the matters that are disputed, for they are not like those principles in clarity and obviousness. Rather, most of them are from what is found in the Book and Sunnah that the falsifier imagines as an objection to what the truth-holder argues, and each of them claims that the interpretation conforming to his school is more appropriate. So they cannot be made as things on which the soundness of Islam depends, so it is not permissible to proceed to takfir because there is great danger. To the explanation of truth in the details when they are considered, even if they are among what there is no disagreement about declaring the opponent a disbeliever, like the origination of the world. How many a believer does not know the meaning of originated and eternal at all and never conceives the hadith of the gathering of bodies, absolutely, but if he considers that, then if he does not believe, he becomes a disbeliever. And the answer: We are certain that some of them have stopped at the details, even if not all of them are like that. His saying: (with the people of summary) means those of summary, for they are not able to refine the proof.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument establishing that no one from the people of the qibla (i.e., Muslims) should be declared a disbeliever for holding mistaken views on disputed theological matters. The author begins with the principle that the soundness of Islam does not depend on knowing the truth in such matters, and error in them does not harm the reality of Islam. He supports this by noting that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not investigate the detailed beliefs of his companions on these issues. An objection is raised: perhaps the Prophet knew they knew them in summary, so he did not investigate. The author refutes this as stubborn denial, pointing out that the Bedouins who came to the Prophet were not all aware of detailed theological points (e.g., that God knows by knowledge not by essence, that He is visible in the hereafter, that He is not a body, that He creates all actions). The author then distinguishes between principles necessary for prophethood (knowledge and power) and disputed matters. He quotes Imam al-Razi, who uses a vivid example from nature to show that the proofs of the fundamentals of Islam are clear and accessible to ordinary people, unlike complex disputed issues that have conflicting interpretations. Therefore, declaring disbelief is not permissible. Then, a further objection is considered: even matters of consensus like the creation of the world require knowledge? The author answers that some people do have knowledge of the details, but not all, and the lack of knowledge in some does not entail disbelief unless they reject after understanding. The passage ends with a gloss on the phrase 'people of summary' (as-hab al-jumal), explaining that they are those who cannot refine the proof.

Key Terms
أهل القبلة
تكفير
أصول الإسلام
إجمال
تفصيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any error in theological details makes one a disbeliever.
Correction: The passage clarifies that only rejection of fundamentals after clear proof leads to disbelief; error in disputed details does not harm one's Islam.

Checkpoint
Why did the Prophet not investigate the detailed beliefs of his companions according to the author?
A) Because they were all scholars of kalam
B) Because detailed knowledge is not required for soundness of Islam
C) Because the Prophet was not concerned with theology
D) Because the companions all agreed on the details

Key Takeaway
The soundness of a person's Islam is not affected by error in non-essential theological details.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever looked down on another Muslim because they held a different view on a theological detail? How does this lesson challenge you to examine your heart and actions?
?
When you encounter a believer with a non-essential doctrinal error, what would it look like to treat them as a full Muslim despite that error? Are you willing to extend that grace?
?
Is there a theological issue you have treated as more important than the Quran and Sunnah treat it? What would it mean for you to realign your priorities with the Prophet's example of silence on such issues?

Refuting the Objection: Summary Knowledge vs. Detailed Ignorance
Author presents an objection and refutes it with historical evidence and a crucial distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection that the Prophet knew the companions had summary knowledge, and the distinction between beliefs necessary for prophethood and those that are not.

Core Idea
Summary knowledge of fundamentals suffices; detailed ignorance of theological specifics does not harm faith.

After stating the principle, the author anticipates an objection: perhaps the Prophet knew that the companions had summary knowledge, so he did not need to investigate. The author rebuts this by pointing to historical reality—the Bedouins were ignorant of detailed attributes—and distinguishes between beliefs essential for establishing prophethood (like God's knowledge and power) and those that are not. This sharpens the original argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection beginning with 'If it is said: Perhaps he knew from them that they knew in summary...'
2
Read the refutation
Read the author's response starting with 'We say: What you mentioned is stubborn denial...'
Pay attention to the Bedouin example.
3
Understand the distinction
Note how the author separates knowledge of God's existence and power (necessary for prophethood) from detailed attributes (not necessary).

المرصد الثالث - المقصد الخامس : الاتفاق على أنه لا يكفر أحد من أهل القبلة تلك صحة دين الإسلام لا تتوقف على معرفة الحق في تلك المسائل و ( أن الخطأ فيها ليس قادحاً في حقيقة الإسلام إذا لو توقفت عليها وكان الخطأ قادحاً في الحقيقة لوجب أن يبحث عن كيفية اعتقادهم فيها، لكن لم يجر حديث شيء منها في زمانه عليه السلام ولا في زمانهم أصلاً ) فإن قيل : لعله عليه السلام عرف منهم ذلك ) أي كونهم عالمين بها إجمالا ) فلم يبحث عنها ) لذلك ) كما لم يبحث عن علمهم بعلمه وقدرته مع وجوب اعتقادهما)، وما ذلك إلا لعلمه بأنهم عالمون على طريق الجملة بأنه تعالى عالم ،قادر، فكذا الحال في تلك المسائل (قلنا :) ما ذكرتموه ) مكابرة ) لأنا نعلم أن الأعراب الذين جاؤوا إليه عليه السلام ما كانوا كلهم عالمين بأنه تعالى عالم بالعلم لا بالذات، وأنه مرئي في الدار الآخرة وأنه ليس بجسم ولا مكان وجهة وأنه قادر على أفعال العباد كلها وأنه موجد لها بأسرها، فالقول بأنهم كانوا عالمين بها مما علم فساده بالضرورة (و) أما ( العلم والقدرة ) فيهما ( مما يتوقف عليه ثبوت نبوته لتوقف دلالة المعجزة عليهما ( فكان الاعتراف ) والعلم ( بها ) أي بالنبوة ( دليلاً للعلم بها ، ولو إجمالاً فلذلك لم يبحث عنهما، قال الإمام الرازي: الأصول التي يتوقف عليها صحة نبوة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم أدلتها على ما يليق بأصحاب الجمل ظاهرة فإن من دخل بستاناً ورأى أزهاراً حادثة بعد أن لم تكن ثم رأى عنقود عنب قد اسود جميع حباته إلا حبة واحدة مع تساوي نسبة الماء والهواء وحر الشمس إلى جميع تلك الحبات فإنه يضطر إلى العلم بأن محدثه فاعل مختار لأن دلالة الفعل المحكم على علم فاعله واختياره ضرورية ودلالة المعجزة على صدق المدعى ضرورية أيضاً وإذا عرف هذه الأصول أمكن العلم بصدق الرسول فثبت أن أصول الإسلام جلية وأن أدلتها مجملة واضحة فلذلك لم يبحث عنها بخلاف المسائل التي اختلف فيها فإنها في الظهور والجلاء ليست مثل تلك الأصول بل أكثرها مما ورد في الكتاب والسنة ما يتخيله المبطل معارضاً لما يحتج به المحق فيها، وكل واحد منهما يدعي أن التأويل المطابق لمذهبه أولى فلا يمكن جعلها مما يتوقف عليه صحة الإسلام فلا يجوز الإقدام على التكفير إذ فيه خطر عظيم . إلى بيان الحق في التفاصيل عند ملاحظتها وإن كانت مما لا خلاف في تكفير المخالف فيها كحدوث العالم، فكم من مؤمن لم يعرف معنى الحادث والقديم أصلا ولم يخطر بباله حديث حشر الأجساد ،قطعاً، لكن إذا لاحظ ذلك فلو لم يصدق كان كافراً. والجواب : إنا نقطع بأن منهم من وقف على التفاصيل وإن لم يكن كلهم كذلك . قوله : ( بأصحاب الجمل ) أي أرباب الإجمال فإنهم لا يقدرون على تنقيح الدليل
The third observation - the fifth aim: Agreement that no one of the people of the qibla is declared a disbeliever. That. The soundness of the religion of Islam does not depend on knowing the truth in those matters, and (that error in them is not a defect in the reality of Islam, because if it depended on them and error were a defect in the reality, then it would be necessary to investigate the nature of their belief in them, but no mention of any of them occurred in his time, peace be upon him, nor in their time at all.) If it is said: Perhaps he, peace be upon him, knew from them that (i.e., that they knew them in summary) so he did not investigate them (for that reason) just as he did not investigate their knowledge of His knowledge and power despite the obligation of believing in them, and that is only because he knew that they know in a summary way that He, exalted, is knowing, powerful, so the case is the same in those matters. (We say:) What you mentioned is stubborn denial, because we know that the Bedouins who came to him, peace be upon him, were not all knowing that He, exalted, is knowing through knowledge not by essence, and that He is visible in the hereafter, and that He is not a body, nor place, nor direction, and that He is powerful over all the actions of servants, and that He is the creator of them entirely. So the claim that they knew them is known to be false necessarily. And (as for) knowledge and power, they are (among what the establishment of his prophethood depends on, because the indication of the miracle depends on them), so acknowledgment (and knowledge) of them (i.e., of prophethood) is a proof of knowledge of them, even if in summary. Therefore he did not investigate them. Imam al-Razi said: The principles on which the soundness of the prophethood of Muhammad, peace be upon him, depends—their proofs are apparent in a manner befitting the people of summary. For whoever enters a garden and sees flowers newly originated after not being, then sees a cluster of grapes whose all grapes have blackened except one grape, despite the equal proportion of water, air, and sun heat to all those grapes, he is compelled to know that its originator is a free agent, because the indication of the precise action to the knowledge and choice of its agent is necessary, and the indication of the miracle to the truthfulness of the claimant is also necessary. When these principles are known, knowledge of the truthfulness of the messenger is possible. So it is established that the principles of Islam are clear and their proofs are summary and clear. Therefore he did not investigate them, unlike the matters that are disputed, for they are not like those principles in clarity and obviousness. Rather, most of them are from what is found in the Book and Sunnah that the falsifier imagines as an objection to what the truth-holder argues, and each of them claims that the interpretation conforming to his school is more appropriate. So they cannot be made as things on which the soundness of Islam depends, so it is not permissible to proceed to takfir because there is great danger. To the explanation of truth in the details when they are considered, even if they are among what there is no disagreement about declaring the opponent a disbeliever, like the origination of the world. How many a believer does not know the meaning of originated and eternal at all and never conceives the hadith of the gathering of bodies, absolutely, but if he considers that, then if he does not believe, he becomes a disbeliever. And the answer: We are certain that some of them have stopped at the details, even if not all of them are like that. His saying: (with the people of summary) means those of summary, for they are not able to refine the proof.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument establishing that no one from the people of the qibla (i.e., Muslims) should be declared a disbeliever for holding mistaken views on disputed theological matters. The author begins with the principle that the soundness of Islam does not depend on knowing the truth in such matters, and error in them does not harm the reality of Islam. He supports this by noting that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not investigate the detailed beliefs of his companions on these issues. An objection is raised: perhaps the Prophet knew they knew them in summary, so he did not investigate. The author refutes this as stubborn denial, pointing out that the Bedouins who came to the Prophet were not all aware of detailed theological points (e.g., that God knows by knowledge not by essence, that He is visible in the hereafter, that He is not a body, that He creates all actions). The author then distinguishes between principles necessary for prophethood (knowledge and power) and disputed matters. He quotes Imam al-Razi, who uses a vivid example from nature to show that the proofs of the fundamentals of Islam are clear and accessible to ordinary people, unlike complex disputed issues that have conflicting interpretations. Therefore, declaring disbelief is not permissible. Then, a further objection is considered: even matters of consensus like the creation of the world require knowledge? The author answers that some people do have knowledge of the details, but not all, and the lack of knowledge in some does not entail disbelief unless they reject after understanding. The passage ends with a gloss on the phrase 'people of summary' (as-hab al-jumal), explaining that they are those who cannot refine the proof.

Key Terms
مكابرة
فاعل مختار
إجمال
تفصيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Summary knowledge of details is sufficient to avoid disbelief in every case.
Correction: The author shows that summary knowledge of fundamentals is sufficient, but detailed ignorance of attributes is not harmful; the objection's attempt to generalize is refuted.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the example of the Bedouins a refutation of the objection?
A) Because the Bedouins were all scholars
B) Because they clearly lacked detailed knowledge of God's attributes
C) Because they denied the Prophet's prophethood
D) Because they were not asked about their beliefs

Key Takeaway
Ignorance of detailed theological attributes does not harm one's faith, while summary knowledge of fundamentals is sufficient.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own religious practice, do you ever focus on debating minor theological details (like God's essence or attributes) at the expense of the simple faith in God and His Messenger that the Bedouins had? What would it take for you to return to that simplicity today?
?
The author labels the objection as 'stubborn denial'. Is there any belief you hold about God or religion that you cling to out of pride or habit, rather than because it is clearly taught by revelation and reason? If so, what step can you take this week to examine it honestly?
?
The Bedouins were considered believers despite their ignorance of detailed attributes. How does this challenge your attitude towards other Muslims who may lack detailed theological knowledge? Are you willing to prioritize practical faith over intellectual superiority? What one change can you make today to embody this humility?

Al-Razi's Analogy: Clarity of Fundamental Proofs
Imam al-Razi's analogy and the author's concluding argument against takfir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Razi's analogy demonstrating that the proofs of Islamic fundamentals are clear and accessible, unlike disputed matters, and why takfir is impermissible in such disputes.

Core Idea
The fundamental proofs of Islam are as clear as seeing a blackened grape cluster in a garden.

Imam al-Razi provides a vivid analogy to illustrate that the foundational principles of Islam are self-evident to any rational person. This stands in contrast to disputed theological details, which require careful reasoning and are subject to misinterpretation. The author concludes that declaring someone a disbeliever over such disputes is dangerous and unwarranted, even if some matters (like the creation of the world) are clear in detail after reflection.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Razi's analogy
Read the analogy of the garden and the grape cluster. Understand how it shows that a precise action implies a knowing, free agent.
2
Understand the implication for Islam's fundamentals
Al-Razi argues that the principles on which prophethood depends have proofs that are 'apparent in a manner befitting the people of summary'.
3
See the conclusion about takfir
Read the final part where the author forbids takfir in disputed matters, and note the clarification about detailed knowledge being required after reflection.

According to Imam al-Razi's analogy, what does the precise difference in the grape cluster indicate?
A) That the garden was planted by chance

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Al-Razi's analogy shows that even a simple observation compels certainty. Do you have that same compelling certainty in the foundations of your faith? If not, what step will you take today to strengthen it?
?
The author warns of 'great danger' in takfir. Consider a time when you spoke harshly about someone's belief. Will you seek forgiveness and commit to learning the principles that protect the unity of Muslims, even when differences arise?

Refuting Takfir of Rawafid and Khawarij
Sanusi refutes the reasons for declaring Rawafid and Khawarij disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main arguments used to declare Rawafid and Khawarij disbelievers and the counterarguments based on general vs. specific praise, the status of ahad hadiths, and conditional praise.

Core Idea
Not all criticism of companions amounts to disbelief; the Quran's praise is general.

This passage examines two reasons given for declaring the Rawafid and Khawarij outside the fold of Islam. The first concerns slandering the companions, and the author offers nuanced refutations. The second invokes consensus. This lesson unpacks these theological arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally.
Notice that the passage presents two distinct arguments followed by responses.
2
Identify the first argument and its refutation
Find where the author states that slandering companions is disbelief because the Quran and hadith praise them. Then see how he refutes this: the Quran's praise is general, not specific; hadiths are ahad; praise is conditional.
The refutation has three parts: general praise, ahad hadiths, conditional praise.
3
Examine the second argument
Identify the second argument: consensus that whoever declares companions disbelievers is himself a disbeliever. Notice that the author presents it without refutation, implying acceptance.
This argument is short and not contested.
4
Reflect on the implications
Think about how these distinctions protect Muslims from hasty takfir. The author uses careful reasoning to limit the application of takfir.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع من تلك الأبحاث قد كفر الروافض والخوارج بوجوه : الأول : أن القدح في أكابر الصحابة الذين شهد لهم القرآن والأحاديث الصحيحة بالتزكية والإيمان تكذيب للقرآن وللرسول حيث أثنى عليهم وعظمهم فيكون كفرا قلنا : لا ثناء عليهم خاصة أي لاثناء في القرآن على واحد من الصحابة بخصوصه، وهؤلاء قد اعتقدوا أن من قدحوا فيه ليس داخلاً في الثناء العام الوارد فيه وإليه أشار بقوله : ولاهم داخلون فيه عندهم فلا يكون تكذيباً للقرآن، وأما الأحاديث الواردة في تزكية بعض معين من والشهادة لهم بالجنة فمن قبيل الآحاد فلا يكفر المسلم بإنكارها، أو نقول : ذلك الثناء عليهم وتلك الشهادة لهم مقيدان بشرط سلامة العاقبة ولم توجد عندهم فلا يلزم تكذيبهم للرسول، الثاني : الإجماع منعقد من الأمة على تكفير من كفر الصحابة.
The fourth: From these discussions: they declared the Rawafid (Rafidites) and Khawarij disbelievers on several grounds: The first: That slandering the major companions, whom the Quran and authentic hadiths have testified to with praise and faith, is a denial of the Quran and the Messenger, because He praised and honored them, so it is disbelief. We said: There is no praise specifically for them, i.e., there is no praise in the Quran for any individual companion in particular. And these [Rawafid and Khawarij] believe that the one they slandered is not included in the general praise that occurs in it. And he indicated by his statement: 'And they are not included in it according to them, so it is not a denial of the Quran. As for the hadiths that have come praising a specific individual and testifying to Paradise, they are singular (ahad) reports, and a Muslim is not declared a disbeliever by denying them. Or we say: that praise upon them and that testimony are conditional upon a good ending, and it is not present according to them, so they are not charged with denial of the Messenger. The second: The consensus of the community is established on declaring disbelievers those who declare the companions disbelievers.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage addresses two arguments used to declare Rafidites and Kharijites disbelievers. The first argument is that they slander companions praised by Quran and hadith. The answer: the Quran's praise is general, not specific to any one companion; the slandered individual may not be included in that general praise. The hadiths are ahad (solitary), which do not necessitate takfir upon denial. Alternatively, the praise is conditional on ending well, and these individuals may not have that end. The second argument is a consensus that whoever declares the companions disbelievers is himself a disbeliever. This argument is presented without refutation, implying it is accepted.

Key Terms
الروافض
الخوارج
الصحابة
الآحاد
التزكية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any criticism of a companion instantly makes one a disbeliever.
Correction: The Quran's praise is general, not specific to individuals, and hadiths about specific companions are ahad, so denying them does not necessitate takfir. Moreover, praise is conditional on a good ending.

Checkpoint
What is one of the reasons given against declaring Rawafid disbelievers?
A) The Quran specifically praises each companion
B) The hadiths about companions are all mutawatir
C) The praise in the Quran is general, not specific
D) They do not slander companions

Key Takeaway
The author defends against takfir by arguing that Quranic praise of companions is general, not specific, and that ahad hadiths do not necessitate disbelief upon denial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed a whole group of Muslims because of a minority within them? How does Sanusi’s refusal to generalize praise challenge your readiness to condemn? Will you now examine the basis for your judgments before assuming disbelief?
?
When you hear criticism of early Muslims or contemporary scholars, do you react with instant rejection or do you carefully check if the Quran and hadith specifically address that person? This lesson forces you to admit that general praise does not cover every individual. Are you willing to hold your own certainties with that same uncertainty?
?
If the Quran’s praise is conditional on a good ending, what makes you so sure of your own standing? How does this truth—that no one’s final state is guaranteed—change the way you look at those you consider in error? Commit tonight to pray for humility rather than self-righteousness.
